asked the Minister of Mass Media and Information and Minister of Enterprise Development and Investment Promotion:

(a) Will he inform this House,-

(i) the number of TV stations that are in operation in the country;

(ii) the number of licences issued to operate TV stations that have still not come into operation; and

(iii) the frequencies of their telecasting TV stations?

(b) Is he aware that the Government had introduced taxes to discourage the foreign TV films flowing to the country with the intention of assisting the local film industry?

(c) Will he state,-

(i) whether it has achieved its objective;

(ii) if so, where and how these benefits have been obtained; and

(iii) the amount that has been paid by each TV station per month since the tax was imposed to-date?

(d) Will he also state,-

(i) the other taxes that have been imposed on these TV stations; and

(ii) the amount earned by the Government for the last 12 months separately?

(e) If not, why?

SRI LANKA RAILWAYS : OPERATIONAL LOSS 0083/09 2. ( ) (The Hon. Lakshman Nipunaarachchi) - (1) : () 2008 3,671 22.4 ? () 4,553 5.9 2008 ? () (i) ; (ii) ; ? () , ?

? ( ) , ?

asked the Minister of Transport: (a) Is he aware of the fact that the Sri Lanka Railways has had its total income increased to Rs. 3,671 million in the year 2008, an increase of 22.4 per cent due to the increase in train fares? (b) Will he admit that the operational loss of the Sri Lanka Railways has increased to Rs. 4,553 million, an increase of 5.9 per cent in the year 2008, in spite of the above increase in the total income? (c) Will he state- (i) the reasons for the Sri Lanka Railways to sustain such a huge loss, in spite of the increase of income due to increase in train fares; and (ii) the steps he has taken in his capacity as the Minister in charge of the subject to change this situation? (d) If not, why?

CENTRAL BANK OF SRI LANKA

Communications Department 30, Janadhipathi Mawatha, Colombo 01, Sri Lanka Tel: 2477424, 2477423, 2477311 E-mail:dcommuatications@cbs. lk, communications@cbsl.lk Web:www.cbsl.gov.;k

Press Release Issued by Economic Research Department Date 27-07-2009

I'will Approves USD 2.6 billion Stand-By Arrangement Facility for Sri Lanka

The Executive Board of the International Monetary Fund (IMF) on 24 July 2009 approved a 20 month Stand-By Arrangement (SBA) facility of SDR 1.65 billion (approximately USD 2.6 billion), to Sri Lanka as a Balance of Payment (BOP) support. This accounts for 400 per cent of the country's current quota with the Fund and is the highest ever facility offered by the IMF to Sri Lanka Immediately on approval of the facility, the first tranche amounting SDR 206.7 million (approximately USD 322 million) was made available to Sri Lanka, and this is the single largest disbursement the country had thus far received from the IMF. The remaining amount will be disbursed in seven tranches subject to the quarterly reviews on economic performance of the country.

Despite the unprecedented increase in fuel and commodity prices, particularly during the first half of the year, economic fundamentals of Sri Lanka had been improving steadily until the third quarter of 2008. However, by end 2008, the BOP turned into a deficit and external official reserves dropped significantly as a result of several adverse factors, such as, the sudden withdrawal of investment in Treasury Bill and Bonds by foreign investors, the hasty claims on short term credit facilities that were quite freely available for petroleum imports, the acute drying-up of commercial financing required for counterpart fund for the implementation of foreign funded projects under the public investment programme and severe valuation losses arising from the sharp depreciation of major international currencies against US dollar. Such factors have exerted an unforeseen and unfavorable pressure on the country's BOP and led to a substantial decline in external reserves.

In that context, in March 2009, Sri Lanka sought a SBA facility with exceptional access from the IMF amounting to USD 1.9 billion, 300 percent of country's current quota. In response to the request, a team of IMF officials visited Sri Lanka in late March to assess the impact of the global financial crisis on Sri Lanka and to consider as to whether Sri Lanka was in need of such assistance. The IMF officials has several key meetings with various government and non-government organizations to obtain first hand information. Further, the Sri Lankan delegation to the IMF spring Meetings held several rounds of discussions with senior staff of the IMF. A Safeguards Assessment mission from the IMF also visited

Sri Lanka to evaluate the reliability of information, procedures and processes of internal controls and concluded that the Central Bank of Sri Lanka employs a relatively strong framework of safeguards. However, despite the successful completion of all technical level negotiations and the finalization of the content of the Letter of intent in April 2009, there was a delay in taking the SBA facility for discussion by the Executive Board of the IMF. In the ensuing period, the Central Bank of Sri Lanka was able to build up official reserves by about US dollars 500 million on a net basis after supplying foreign exchange to meet all government debt service obligations as well. Further, inflation was brought down to below one per cent by end June 2009 from 28 per cent in June 2008. With the ending of the decades long conflict with the LTTE in May 2009, a staff mission from the IMF arrived once again in Sri Lanka in early July, to understand the new environment and update the Program accordingly. Upon completion of the mission negotiations, the IMF indicated the SBA facility would be taken for discussion by the Executive Board on 24 July 2009 and accordingly, the LOI was signed by the Sri Lankan authorities on 16 July 2009, with the key objectives under the SBA Program being to rebuild external reserves further, while strengthening the country's fiscal position and the domestic financial system. The approval of the SBA facility on 24 July 2009 is an endorsement of country's economic policies by the IMF as all macroeconomic policies and targets under the 20 month Program are in the with policies already implemented and announced by the authorities. The Government budget deficit for 2009 is expected to be 7 per cent of GDP under the Program. The fiscal consolidation path accommodates expenditure for relief, rehabilitation and reconstruction of the conflict affected areas while protecting social expenditure such as expenditure for health, education and Samurdi payments. It is also strongly believed that the endorsement of the Sri Lankan authorities policies by the IMF would boost investor confidence in Sri Lanka and enhance the countrys ability to attract local and foreign investment as well as loans from bilateral and multilateral agencies. These investments could be channeled for infrastructure development as well as for the post-conflict reconstruction and relief effort, thereby increasing countrys production and job creation in the long run and lay the foundation for future economic growth and enhance macroeconomic stability. Under the 20-month SBA Program, the final tranche will be disbursed in March 2011. The loan is repayable within 4 years commencing April 2012. The rate of interest of the SBA facility is composed of two components; the service charge and a fixed margin. The service charge is calculated weekly, based on the SDRs rate (which at present is 0.3 per cent per annum) while the fixed margin is 1 per cent per annum for the outstanding loan amount up to 300 percent of the quota. When the outstanding loan amount exceeds 300per cent of the quota, a surcharge of 2 per cent per annum is to be levied. The interest rate of the SBA facility is significantly lower than the prevailing market rates. A schedule of IMF facilities obtained by Sri Lanka during the period 1977 to 2009 is set out in Annexe 1. ( ) (The Hon. Ravi Karunanayake) . , . I am sure, Hon. Minister, you will agree that the IMF loan is only a bridging facility or a structural standby assistance. But, there is also a system for poverty reduction and growth facility. Now, I was pretty surprised when the Minister, the Hon. (Dr.) Sarath Amunugama, was relatively unaware of the situation that

permitted the Government to go into poverty reduction. At this particular moment, you had requested for US Dollars 1.9 billion and they have given you US Dollars 2.6 billion. That is a spectacular performance to many of us as to why such a big amount has been given. However, it is apparent that it is set in a more convoluted manner. You must ensure that the hedging money is also paid because US Dollars 1.9 billion plus US Dollars 700 million is US Dollars 2.6 billion. Whether it is said or not, these are things that would happen because it is in arbitration. The next most important thing is that you have gone to the IMF which is certainly transparent as opposed to the HSBC and the ICICI Bank. You know that taking a loan from a commercial bank is not all that healthy from a country's perspective. Why we said, do not take it from the HSBC is because for US Dollars 500 million at 8.5 per cent fixed interest, it is roughly US Dollars 42 million a year. But, if you look at the IMF loan of US Dollars 2.6 billion at 0.03 per cent interest you are not going to pay more than US Dollars 7.2 million a year. You could see that the interest of the HSBC loan is almost six times bigger. The interest of the IMF is 60 per cent less than the HSBC loans. So, this is what we told you. But, when we told you to go to the IMF some people laughed; may not be you, may not be the Hon. Dinesh Gunawardena but certainly the morons who basically think otherwise, or those who do not think on the same lines on a commercial basis of how to run a country. Now , but there is no way of doing any development activities. You can utilize the monies that are there and substitute other monies for different things. But, you cannot use the IMF money because that is there to support you only when the reserves are at absolutely low levels. Coming back to that particular point, what is the most important thing that has got to be done? You should ensure that you take a poverty reduction growth facility loan on that particular basis. When Chandrika Kumaratunga ran the economy down and when the Hon. (Prof.) G.L. Peiris and all of you came along, we were placed with a 1.6 per cent negative growth. What did we do? When the reserves were not there and when things were bad all over, we had to go to the IMF. But, even then, we got US Dollars 200 million and we spent only US Dollars 28 million. That is how it was. By that time we got the economy up and running and there was no necessity to go for other things. You have sent back only 20,000 people for the last two months and you are saying that the other 80 per cent or 280,000 people would be sent back within three months. So, your own position is self-contradictory. Also, look at the absolutely despicable standards

prevailing there. There, it is raining. You have not allowed the Opposition Members to go and see them. There is no sanitation; there are no toilet facilities; there are no water facilities; immunization programmes are not implemented; there is a breakout of epidemics. You have to ensure that proper measures are taken. So, Hon. Minister, it is more a human tragedy that is taking place there rather than anything else. I think scant respect is being paid to these people. After all, they are citizens of this country. You will lure them to vote at the next election, but you do not seem to be doing anything and I do not think anyone is keen to get the work done and finish off. Then, Hon. Minister, the next one is, you expect to increase the income of this country. At the present moment, the revenue is around 12 per cent of GDP. You are saying that you want to increase it by another 2 per cent. There was an interpretation given by the Hon. Deputy Minister of Finance and Planning to say that this is going to be a new tax base coming into the net. Well and good, if that is the case. But, if that is not the case, you still have to meet the conditions. So, on that score, you will be saying, We are sorry. We could not get the file. So, as a result, we have got to increase the revenues. Or is it your intention to take only one or two instalments and then tell them, Okay, we have enough. Now, we do not want your money. So, you can go off with that? But then, for that, there must be an effective investment scheme coming on. The trade gap for the first six months is roughly about Rs. 1.3 billion. It is estimated to be about Rs. 3 billion. So, if there is going to be a trade gap of Rs. 3 billion, with the foreign remittances coming into this country at Rs. 2 billion, you still have a shortage of about Rs. 1 billion. So, are you going to get another commercial loan? I am informed that you are going after another US Dollars 800 million in order to ensure that you beef up the reserves mandated by the IMF. But, you will have to substantiate that. There is no point in saying that that is in theory. How are you going to achieve it in practice? Otherwise, you are going to make a bad case worse with the conditions that you have entered into. I do not want to talk too much on the CEB because it has already been mentioned that there have been increases. Today what is happening? The Hon. Ranjith Siyabalapitiya has stated in todays Daily News, I quote: reserves up by 40 per cent But, on the other side, you are allowing for Treasury Bills. You are paying 11 per cent to the foreigners who come to invest because you have opened the door for them to invest in 10 per cent of the Treasury Bills. Today the international bonds are at LIBOR plus one per cent. Instead of paying one per cent, you are paying 11 per cent to the foreigners. So, you are allowing the foreigners to come, rape us and go out at any time they want. Is this what you call "reserve development"? ( ) (The Presiding Member) , .

2009 18 1055 1056

( ) (The Hon. Ravi Karunanayake) , .

It is worse than privatization. You allow them to come and take a huge benefit in respect of the interest factor. It is almost ten times of what is allowed in the normal international markets as of today, and then you tell them, Okay, go off. Look at the pensions that they are trying to target. By the year 2015, you will have to have Rs. 15 billion per month as payments for the pensions. Today it is Rs. 7.2 billion. They are asking us as to how we are going to overcome this problem. Then, there is the problem of hedging. You have not brought those guys - the Governor of the Central Bank and the other officials - into line. They took you all to the cleaners. There is an arbitration going on. As I said before, this is the reason as to why they have given an additional facility for you. That is, to ensure that you basically pay and honour the commercial commitments as a sovereign government. You cannot suddenly say, Go to hell. You cannot go to the Supreme Court and get an injunction. The world turns on and you have to answer. If you look at what Mr. Kato, Deputy Managing Director of IMF as well as Mr. Brain Aitken have said, - because now you are going to open up an office here for him, he is coming here and going to look after everything - there is an absolute paradox between what you are saying and what they are saying in their website. So, at the end of the day you have got to achieve the targets as per what you have signed for. You can put it in any English that you like. You can look at it in any angle that you like. But, finally the targets have to be met. Hon. Minister, you were defending this and trying to get the loan. Look at what is happening to the Labour GSP. Tell us whether it is coming about or not because if that is not going to happen, you will have a bigger trade gap. In another two or three weeks time you will have to highlight whether the benefits of Labour GSP would be accrued to Sri Lanka or not. If not, how is it going to be looked at and why are you losing it out? You are basically going on the basis that you have an absolute right and a must to get it. If you do not get it, then what is going to be the answer? That is why I say, that you must realize that we, Sri Lanka, is a small country in the world. We have got to ensure that we have harmonious international relationships. You can catch more bees with honey than with vinegar. You cannot have the Minister of Foreign Affairs saying one thing, a special Minister saying another thing and in between you are saying, No, both of them are saying this but the real meaning is this. Then again you say, We do not want any Westerners; those were the guys who ruined and robbed our country. So, we will do what we want to do. At the end of the day we have got to look at Sri Lankas sovereignty. We do not need to be

bending to anybody. That, in no way is the stand of the United National Party. But, we must be commercially prudent to ensure tha0t we get what is good for the country.

Look at the IMF loan. We certainly said, This is the way forward. We appreciate it. But, if you had looked at the poverty reduction and growth facility, it would have been desirable to ensure a more favourable disposition with the funds that have been allocated for us. That was what the UNP did. We only utilized an X amount. When they were trying to put unwanted conditions, we rejected those.

2009 18 1059 1060

[. . 1.35]

. . ( ) ( .. - , , ) (The Hon. (Prof.) G.L. Peiris - Minister of Export Development and International Trade and Acting Minister of Posts and Telecommunications)

Venerable Presiding Member, as we look at the provisions in the Agreement that was entered into with the International Monetary Fund, it is absolutely necessary to be objective and not to look at things in an emotional way.

Sri Lanka has been a member of the IMF since 1950 and during that period, on 23 different occasions we have obtained assistance from the IMF. So, that is nothing new. It has happened 23 times since we joined the IMF in 1950. During the last one year, no fewer than 20 countries have obtained assistance from the IMF. When the Government claims that this is the largest sum of money ever to have been put at our disposal by the IMF, it is not an idle boast. It is a statement of fact.

The provision that we have been given is 400 per cent of the country quota and that amounts to US Dollars 2.5 billion. The first tranche has already come into the country. That is about US Dollars 313 million. The way the transaction is structured is such that we are entitled to this money in eight equal instalments. Each instalment is approximately of the value of US Dollars 313 million or SDR 206 million. The final tranche is being paid to Sri Lanka on the 15th of March, 2011. So, the fact of the matter is, it is the largest sum of money that the country has received from the IMF. But, from our point of view, I can sincerely say that the most important consideration is not the quantum of resources. Today it is known that if the Government actually needed this money, it was available to us from several countries on a bilateral basis. That is not a secret. There has been a public statement made to that effect by Mr. Adarsh Kishore, the Executive Director of India in the International Monetary Fund. So, we could have got the money, if we needed, from other sources. But, what really matters here is the overwhelming message of confidence that this transaction sends to the international community. I would like to tell the Hon. Sunil Handunetti and the Hon. Ravi Karunanayake that yesterday - I do not know whether they are aware of this - in one day, Sri Lanka received an inflow of US Dollars 270 million. In one day, that is yesterday, Sri Lanka received US Dollars 270 million. Just consider that objectively. The Hon. Sunil Handunnetti as well as the Hon. Ravi Karunanayake asked, What does this mean to the ordinary people? Will there be development?

, , , . , . . , . ? , . . . . . . . . , . , - 24 - ? 31. . 24 . . . . . - ( ) (The Hon. Ravi Karunanayake) Hon. Minister . . ( .. ) (The Hon. (Prof.) G.L. Peiris)

Please do not interrupt me. I did not interrupt you. On many occasions I was tempted to interrupt you; I could have done that many times. Please allow me to develop my line of argument. -[Interruption.] No, no. I could have proved you factually wrong had I intervened when you were on your feet. Through respect for you and for a Member of Parliament, I did not do that. Now, I must be given that equal facility of developing my own line of argument. I was replying to both the Hon. Sunil Handunnetti and the Hon. Ravi Karunanayake.

. , , . , . . . . The Chamber of Construction Industry . , . . .

6 PL 004315 (2009/08)

1061 1062

. , . ripple effect ? . Lord Keynes said, "At a time like this, pump money into the economy". That is how you generate employment. Let monies flow through every nook and corner of society. There are certain essential conditions which have to be fulfilled before that state of things can be achieved and I say without any hesitation whatsoever that this vast amount of resources that flowed into this land, into Sri Lanka, within the short span of 24 hours, yesterday, US Dollars 270 million equivalent to Sri Lankan Rupees 31,000 million, injects an enormous vitality and confidence into Sri Lankas economy and opens up vistas of opportunity for employment, for trade and for infrastructure development. All this is made possible because of the consequence that is being generated by this transaction. Otherwise, we could have got this money from about three countries. That is a fact. Now, what then does it amount to? It amounts to the fact that this is the most powerful message that can go out to the international community; that Sri Lankas economy is bankable, it is reliable, investors can come here without reluctance or misgivings. As far as international trade is concerned, the parameters of that trade can expand considerably. I do not know whether the Hon. Members are aware, during the last three days the Hilton Hotel and the Cinnamon Grand Hotel have been almost full. I know one case where a foreign delegation came and there was a person who arrived unexpectedly. He found it impossible to get a room at the Hilton Hotel. So, there is an upsurge; during the month of July, tourist arrivals recorded an increase of approximately 15 per cent. So, all these are manifestations of a new threshold of confidence, a threshold of confidence which from the Governments point of view is more important than the quantum of resources to which we have access in consequence of this Agreement. . , " , " . . , , , . ? . . . - - . , " " , , " " . , . Then also the rupee, Venerable Presiding Member, both externally and domestically will achieve a situation of stability. The value of the rupee can be safeguarded by the Government with far greater strength as a direct result of this transaction.

- - 25 , 30 . " " . . . . 40 . . . , , . . . . , " " . . , . ? . , . .

Then, Venerable Presiding Member, as we develop the country, as we open up the economy, this is going to be exceedingly helpful. , '' ''. '' " , . , . , , . Now, that is why the International Monetary Fund has done something quite unique in my experience. During the six years, from 1994 - 2000, twice a year I visited Washington in those days as Deputy Minister of Finance in order to have extensive discussions with the World Bank and the International Monetary Fund. Venerable Presiding Member, on no occasion did this happen at all. At that time, our negotiations were with Mieko Nishimizu who was the Vice-President of the World Bank. Then, the same sort of discussion took place with the International Monetary Fund where the Managing Director Michel Camdessus met me on every occasion when I was in Washington. If I went to Michel Camdessus and said that the Government proposes to control the budget deficit at 6.5 per cent, he would invariably tell me, That is not good enough Minister; you could bring it down a little more, make it 6 per cent. We will not accept 6.5 per cent, make it 6 per cent. Now, here the opposite has happened. The International Monetary Fund is saying, 6.5 per cent is your target. That was a target specifically incorporated into the Budget that was presented to this august Assembly by His Excellency Mahinda Rajapaksa in his capacity as the Minister of Finance. So, that is a target identified by none other than the sovereign Government of Sri Lanka.

[ . . ]

2009 18 1063 1064

Here, you have the unprecedented situation of the International Monetary Fund saying, We do not mind the budget deficit being a little higher. Let it be 7 per cent on this occasion. That is because the IMF realizes that Sri Lanka is at a critical juncture in her contemporary history. There are very high levels of expectations. Unrequited hopes and unfulfilled expectations are very dangerous. That is one of the lessons that we have to learn from political and social history. We are living in an age when new opportunities are opening up before us with the defeat of terrorism, with the eradication of terrorism from Sri Lankan soil and with the gradual disintegration of the vast network, the vast financial apparatus which has been assembled by the LTTE over the years. In my view, the arrest of Kumaran Pathmanathan is every bit as important as the destruction of the leadership of the LTTE by military action. So, all those hopes and expectations are there. The International Monetary Fund readily recognizes that it is necessary to expend larger resources in order to cater for those people and to ensure that those hopes are fulfilled; that there is no disillusionment or disenchantment. That is the reason why for the first time in the history of their dealings with Sri Lanka, they have said, It does not have to be 6.5 per cent. We do not mind the overall budget deficit being at a higher threshold of 7 per cent.

Then, Venerable Presiding Member, there is another point that I would like to make. Nobody must think that this is the oxygen that we require to keep ourselves alive. That is not the case. I would like to tell this honourable Assembly that as of the day this transaction was finally concluded in Washington, that is Friday, 24th of July, the external reserves of this nation stood at US Dollars 1.7 billion. The low-water mark was reached in March this year when the external reserves stood at US Dollars 1.2 billion. Between March and July this year - that is a period of four months - the countrys external reserves rose by US Dollars 500 million. Out of that amount, Venerable Presiding Member, about US Dollars 175 million represented direct inflows from the corporate sector abroad; foreign companies that are coming here to invest. The Malaysian High Commissioner, His Excellency Rosli Ismail, with whom I took part in a discussion at the Sri Lanka-Malaysia Business Council four nights ago, publicly said that some of the largest companies in Malaysia are today looking closely at investment opportunities in Sri Lanka to come here in a big way. People like Bloomberg are already saying that large investors are coming here. People like George Soros are looking at investment opportunities in this country for two reasons, Venerable Presiding Member. One is the environment of stability and tranquility which prevails on the Island after the eradication of terrorism

and the other is the unprecedented degree of political stability which we enjoy today. There never was since 1948 this degree of political stability and obviously it emboldens, it enthuses the investors who are looking at investment opportunities in this land. Then, there are a few other points that I need to respond to. The Hon. Sunil Handunnetti, for whom I have a great respect, was a student when I was the Vice-Chancellor of the University of Colombo. His speeches are always insightful and thoughtful. He presents ideas in a logical and systematic way. Now, one of the points which he made with great emphasis was that this is a programme which has been imposed upon us by the International Monetary Fund. No, that is not so and that is directly contradicted by the phraseology which is used in this Statement which was made by the IMF itself on the 24th of July, out of Washington. The Hon. Ravi Karunanayake quoted in extenso from the Statement made by Mr. Takatoshi Kato, Deputy Managing Director and Acting Chairman of the IMF on behalf of the Managing Director, Mr. Dominique Strauss-Kahn. If the Hon. Sunil Handunnetti were to look at this document, he will notice that several times, three times in the course of this document, the IMF talks of the Governments programme as "the Governments ambitious programme supported by the IMF". That is the phraseology used by the IMF. They give authorship to the Government. It is a Governments programme. It is not the IMF programme. The IMF is supporting this programme because of the confidence that they have in the Government. So, it is not correct to say that this was tailor-made to suit the ideology and the requirements of the IMF and it is also not correct to say as the Hon. Sunil Handunnetti did, that this simply represented some form of security which we could use in order to obtain loans from other sources. Why do we need loans from other sources when this agreement itself generates so much confidence as to persuade investors to send Sri Lankan Rupees 31, 000 million into this country within the short space of 24 hours.

Now, I want to state a few other points, Venerable Presiding Member. One of the matters which has been debated ad nauseam is the question of conditions or no conditions. The Hon. Ravi Karunanayake said that His Excellency the President, the Hon. Ranjith Siyambalapitiya, the Hon. (Dr.) Sarath Amunugama, the Hon. Bandula Gunawardane and myself that at different times we have all spoken of there being no conditions. Nobody ever said that there are no conditions whatsoever. Nowhere in the world is a standby facility or a loan given unconditionally. Then it is a gift. Nobody in their senses would do that. What the Government has consistently insisted upon is that there was no condition that was contrary to; no condition that was incompatible

1065 1066

with the policy of the Government. In other words, there is not one single condition embodied in this document that is in conflict with the conceptual underpinnings of the "Mahinda Chintana". Now, look at some of the criticisms that had been made. There is a criticism that the Board of Investment concessions are going to be phased out. They are going to be phased out; they should be phased out and all governments without exception have categorically stated that it is their intention that BOI concessions should be phased out over time. I was in charge of the BOI for a long time. At that time, that was definitely our view. Under any government, BOI concessions are not given in perpetuity. They are not intended to last for all time because basically there are distortions. What you must aim at is a lower tax regime generally across the board not to give concessions ad hoc to particular people or particular companies. That is a regrettable necessity that may have to be done at certain times. But, it is not to be done for all times. As circumstances change, as social priorities change, you have to re-evaluate, you have to reassess that policy and you have to phase out BOI concessions. That is a desirable thing to do. It is what all governments in this country have believed in and this has nothing to do with any imposition by or any pressure exerted upon us by the International Monetary Fund. Then when we spoke of increasing tax compliance. That again is an essential and desirable thing that we need to do. Otherwise, people who are in the tax net are asked to pay more and more while large numbers of people who ought to be paying taxes get off scot-free. That is obviously not a defensible state of affairs. So, we have said that we will increase tax compliance and we will simplify taxes. Now, the International Monetary Fund has gone out of its way to commend the Government of Sri Lanka for the initiatives that we have taken with regard to the banking system and the appointment of a Tax Commission. This is the first time since 1992 that a Tax Commission is being appointed. Now, here again there is a wrong view that this is going to mean more taxes; that people are going to be burdened more and more. That is not the case, Venerable Presiding Member. It is not a question of having more taxes; it is the question of rationalizing the taxation system. You do not want a plethora of taxes. We want to simplify them that so that there is predictability and certainty. Investors do forward planning. So, they want to make certain that they can make a profit having invested in this country. If we have a multitude of taxes which keep changing all the time, then that disturbs the sense of certainty and predictability which is a condition precedent for attracting substantial investment into this country and that is being specifically commended by the International Monetary Fund. The statement by the IMF commends the Government for the action that was taken with regard to the recapitalization of Seylan Bank and they make the point that otherwise, there

would have been a contagion effect, that stability of the entire banking system would have been affected and they say that the Government of Sri Lanka took action to arrest that by intervening effectively at the proper time. Then, there has been a great deal of discussion about the Ceylon Electricity Board and the Ceylon Petroleum Corporation. If you look at the wording in the Letter of Intent, which says, It is our aim to ensure that by 2011 these two institutions will cease to be a burden on the State, what is wrong with that? That is an aspiration; it is an aim. We must all work towards that. That is not something that the IMF has to tell us to do. That is a matter of elementary financial prudence and of sound public administration. It is something that we have to figure out for ourselves. All governments have been committed to that objective. It is an objective. It may be achieved in toto; it may be achieved substantially. But, that is a goal that we have to work towards. Surely, it is not necessary for the IMF to intimidate us or to exercise some form of duress or coercion in order to persuade us to accept that point of view. It is a self-evident reality which successive governments in this country have accepted without the slightest reluctance or hesitation.

I also need to say, Venerable Presiding Member, that the IMF has taken this position. They have shown this degree of latitude because of their acknowledgement of the very substantial achievements of this Government in respect of the management of our economy under the leadership of his Excellency Mahinda Rajapaksa.

Now, I will not mention the name of the country but they also had extensive negotiations with another country. If you compare the terms and conditions that were imposed on that country with the terms that they imposed on Sri Lanka, there is a vast difference. In the case of the other country that I am thinking of, they put into the agreement very rigid and stringent conditions with regard to the overall budget deficit; they wanted to bring the budget deficit down very much. Then, they wanted to increase the interest rates. They put in very specific conditions about the price of petroleum products in that country. They intervened very vigorously and actively with regard to the policy rate of the Central Bank or the Resource Bank of that country. But, if you contrast those conditions with what they did in respect of Sri Lanka, there is a world of difference. Now, that is not a coincidence - . . . , , .

( ) (The Presiding Member) .

[ . . ]

2009 18 1067 1068

. . ( .. ) (The Hon. (Prof.) G.L. Peiris) , . . , 28 . 2 . . Then, Venerable Presiding Member, in the first quarter of this year, the projected growth of Sri Lankas economy was only at the level of 1.5 per cent. Today, we know that it will be closer to 4 per cent. It would be something between 3.5 and 4 per cent. Some people have also been making a hue and cry about an alleged decline in remittances from abroad. That has not been the case. If you look at the May figures, there has in fact been an increase of 3 per cent. So, the International Monetary Fund has given us credit for all these things and that is why their treatment of Sri Lanka has been in every way different from the manner in which they approached some other countries that were requesting their assistance at this time. I do not wish to take much more time, Venerable Presiding Member. The Hon. Sunil Handunnetti as well as the Hon. Ravi Karunanayake asked, How are you going to reduce the budget deficit to 7 per cent?. It is 7 per cent this year; it will be 5 per cent by 2011. There are lots of ways we can do that. Today, Sri Lanka is in a very favourable situation. Our rubber prices are at the highest possible level; tea prices are increasing; cinnamon prices are increasing. Then, the money that we will be utilizing this year, for example, for the stimulus package for exporters - that is a one-off thing, you are not going to do it every year - so, three years down the road, we will have very substantial savings. It is therefore entirely feasible that the projections can be met. I also want to assure the Hon. Ravi Karunanayake - of course, we have got 400 per cent of the country quota. That is an achievement. That does not necessarily mean that we will utilize the entire 400 per cent. In fact, we now think that we will not need to utilize the entire quota that the IMF has declared us entitled to. We also think at the rate we are going, by the end of the year the Treasury Bill rate can probably be reduced to 9 per cent. So, we can achieve single-digit interest rates by the end of the year. If that is the case, that will be an enormous stimulus and a fillip to local industry. That has been their main impediment and hindrance at this time. So, let me conclude on this note. The Hon. Ravi Karunanayake said, Let us all adopt a collective, mature and responsible attitude to matters connected with the economy. On behalf of the Government, I would entirely endorse that proposition.

, . , . , . IMF . . , " " IMF . , . ; . . ? , , . , . . ," " . , , . , . , . , . , , . . , . , , , . , , ready-made . . , ; ; . , , . , . . ( ) (The Presiding Member) . . . . [. . 4.31] ( )

( - , ) (The Hon. Dew Gunasekara -Minister of Constitutional Affairs and National Integration) , 30 . 10 .

1109 1110

. . , . . . , . . , , . , . , . . . . . . 10 . . . Mr. Presiding Member, I believe that this is the first occasion that a full-day debate is taking place in this House on a loan pledged by the IMF. The Government readily complied with the request of the Opposition since there is nothing sinister, secretive or deceptive as far as the Government is concerned. What is Sri Lankas track record with regard to the IMF loans? Let us not go as far back as 1953 when the people revolted against the then UNP Government condemning the IMF and the WB prescriptions or conditions. In all, there had been 23 occasions on which Sri Lanka sought assistance from the IMF. Since the UNP Government embraced the open economy or neo-liberalism as its economic strategy in 1977, there have been 14 occasions when Sri Lanka had to go with a begging bowl for loans or standby arrangements or drawings or finance facility or structural adjustment facility or poverty reduction facility or emergency assistance facility, whatever the term that was used. Of the 14, except the emergency assistance for natural disasters - tsunami - on all other occasions the UNP was the ruling party. So, no party in power was so closer to IMF and so involved in the IMF loans as the UNP. So, the UNP has no moral right even to question about IMF loans. The total amount drawn by the UNP Government was 1367.9 SDR millions. Let us go back to the most recent occasion and ascertain what type of conditions the UNP government agreed to? In 2001, there was a 10-point Reform Agenda. In 2003, there was a 13-point Reform Agenda. Were there such conditions this time? Not at all. This is the crux of the matter. People are naturally apprehensive about the IMF conditions, because in the past, the conditions imposed by the IMF created massive political upheavals and turmoils

which caused serious labour unrest and even led to the fall of governments. We have our own experience, Sir, in the month of August 1953, when Dudley Senanayake had to resign consequent to the Great Hartal against IMF conditions. Sri Lanka was one of the first countries in the world to react and resist the IMF prescriptions sacrificing eight precious lives. Sir, the working people, in particular, the working class naturally entertain concerns, fears and suspicions whenever the Government seeks assistance from the IMF. This is a natural and logical reaction judging from our past experience. All performance criteria and bench marks on the present occasion are our own, as clearly expressed in our policy framework and the budget speeches stipulated long before the need for IMF facility, did arise. There is nothing new, nothing detrimental, nothing confidential, secretive or deceptive. The people in the recent mandate, at the Provincial Council Election rejected those unfounded allegations and concerns raised by the Opposition Members. They were in fact not related to reality. If they were related to reality, people would have not given an unprecedented victory of 82 per cent in the Monaragala District, the most backward district with only 4 per cent of national GDP. I would now shift to another aspect and that is in relation to the present ground reality of the IMF itself, the subject matter of the Debate. Firstly, the IMF has in practice and effect undergone and is undergoing changes qualitatively in the context of : (1) The nature dimension and gravity of global financial crisis. (2) Changes in the balance of world economic power. The crisis has speeded up the shift in the balance of world economic power. (3) The changing order of the world economy with the emergence of new economic centres. (4) Shifting of world economic centre from the United States to the Continent of Asia. Six Asian countries together have a GDP of US Dollars 17 trillion surpassing US whose current GDP is only US Dollars 13.8 trillion. (5) Higher growth rates of the Asian economies. Asia is the first continent in the world to get out of the recession and global financial crisis. (6) Awakening of the Latin America and its impact on the American Continent and the change in the balance of forces. VII New economic alliances such as BRIC and Shanghai Corporation.

[ ]

2009 18 1111 1112

Sir, secondly, in consequence of the above-mentioned changes, the US is fast losing its dominance in the IMF. Its voting percentage is reduced to 16.8 per cent and there is a growing demand for readjustment of those existing voting percentage by the new emerging countries. The USA and the OECD together now account for only 48.8 per cent. Countries like Japan, South Korea, Canada and sometimes even Australia, the Netherlands and Belgium take moderate and independent positions in the context of the ongoing changes in the world economy. Thirdly, the US Dollar is on the decline in its role as the international exchange reserve. The dollar now accounts for only 65 per cent of the worlds exchange reserves. The US has become the biggest debtor. The US is no longer the biggest producer in the world - but, of course it is the biggest consumer - whose place has been taken over by China. China owns one-third of the US Bonds and even one-third of the world exchange reserves. The developing countries own 75 per cent of the world's exchange reserves, of which China owns one-third. These are the realities of the day, which neither the Members of the UNP and the JVP nor the TNA are aware of. Fourthly, the IMF itself has run into a crisis. Recently, the IMF had to sell 403 tons of its gold for the purchase of dollars. China has come to her assistance, pledging US Dollars 50 billion on IMF Bonds in order to boost the Funds capacity. SDRs owned by the IMF account for only 1 per cent of the world's exchange reserves. The IMF is no longer in a position to place those political conditions to the developing countries as they did all these years, when the US was dominant in the IMF. As a result, the Washington Consensus has become redundant and inoperative. Fifthly, today the sources of funds are in Asia and the Middle East even though those countries have no voice in the IMF. ( ) (The Presiding Member) , . ( ) ( The Hon. Dew Gunasekara) , . Most of our Opposition Members either have no knowledge of these new developments or realities or pretend not to know them or are completely ignorant of these ongoing changes. Sixthly, Sir, this time the IMFs offer is in the form of a stimulus package. It was never mentioned in the House during this whole Debate. It is a form of a stimulus package offered consequent to a decision taken by the

G-20 and not the G-7, which at its session on 2nd April, 2009, deliberated on the impending global financial crisis and considered as to how the developing countries affected by it could be assisted. The G-20 authorized the IMF to issue US Dollars 250 billion in new SDRs. This augmented its foreign reserves, obviating its need to go for lending and this really helped the developing countries which have gone for loans from the commercial sector. This time the IMF requested Sri Lanka to apply for assistance totally under different circumstances. That is why those formal conditions, which they used to impose, are absent. So, the circumstances have changed. The IMF itself is compelled to change its coercive role and drop its inherent big-power arrogance. The world economy, the economic order and the balance of the world economic power are all changing. ( ) (The Presiding Member) , . . ( ) ( The Hon. Dew Gunasekara)

Sir, the main objective of the IMF assistance was to improve the balance of payment potential of Sri Lanka. Why was it needed? Because of two main factors: the first is, our reserves were dwindling due to factors beyond our control and the second is, we were in a state of war, fighting terrorism which warranted a massive expenditure from the point of view of foreign exchange. By virtue of the new economic strategy of 2005 and onwards, we have been taking positive, effective measures on agriculture, domestic food production, infrastructure development, rural economy, regional development, SME sector, flexible foreign policy application, search for alternative sources of funds and we were not so bad as some other developing countries. ( ) (The Presiding Member) , . ( ) ( The Hon. Dew Gunasekara)

Sir, where the JVP has gone wrong is that they are unable to comprehend the new realities of the world economy. Looking for solutions in the theory of economics or books on economics will not take you anywhere. It is necessary to understand the political economy. Take a Marxist view to understand the political economy, which is undergoing transformation throughout the world. Thank you very much.

Background Report The last Census covering the whole Island was taken in 1981 which was 28 years ago. A Census was to have been conducted in 1991 but it could not be undertaken in the context of the situation prevailing at the time. The next Census was conducted in 2001. That too was done in 18 districts only. Census date are thus unavailable in respect of the remaining districts in the North and East other than the district of Ampara. Again in 2007 a special enumeration was carried out covering Eastern Province and the District of Jaffna. This special enumeration could not be carried out in the districts of Vavuniya, Mullativu, Mannar and Kilinochchi in the context of the situation prevailing at the time. Hence no date are available in respect of those districts since 1981. A population Census or a full enumeration of population would have been the ideal source to determine the extent of the distribution of demographic data such as Age, Gender, Nationality and Religion. Even though on certain occasions, estimates could prepared on the basis of the Census carried out, no unbiased extimates could be arrived at through such enumerations in the absence of recent base data.

Subscriptions : The annual subscription for Official Report of Hansard is Rs. 2,178. A single copy of Hansard is available for Rs. 18.15. (Postage Rs. 2.50) Copies can be obtained by remitting in advance an annual subscription fee to the SUPERINTENDENT, GOVERNMENT PUBLICATIONS BUREAU, No. 132, Maya Avenue, Kirulapone, Colombo 5. The fee should reach him on or before November 30 each year . Late applications for subscriptions will not be accepted.
